style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcdcdc">Front office</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owner(s)</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Peter_Angelos" title="Peter Angelos">Peter Angelos</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Manager</th><td>\nVacant</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\nVacant</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Baltimore Orioles</b> are an American professional <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore, Maryland</a>. As one of the AL\'s original eight charter franchises when the league was established in 1901, this particular franchise spent its first year as a major league club in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>, as the <b>Milwaukee Brewers</b> (not related to the second current Brewers franchise there) before moving to <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a>, to become the <b><a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a></b>. After 52 often-beleaguered years in St. Louis, the franchise was purchased in November 1953 by a syndicate of Baltimore business and civic interests led by attorney/civic activist <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Miles" title="Clarence Miles">Clarence Miles</a> and Mayor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_D%27Alesandro_Jr." title="Thomas D&#39;Alesandro Jr.">Thomas D\'Alesandro Jr.</a> The team\'s current majority owner is lawyer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Angelos" title="Peter Angelos">Peter Angelos</a>.\n</p><p>The Orioles adopted their team name in honor of the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_oriole" title="Baltimore oriole">official state bird of Maryland</a>; it had also been used by several previous major and minor league baseball clubs in Baltimore, including another AL charter member franchise also named the "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Yankees" title="History of the New York Yankees">Baltimore Orioles</a>," which moved north in 1903 to eventually become the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_baseball_nicknames" title="List of baseball nicknames">Nicknames</a> for the team include the  <b>"O\'s"</b> and the <b>"Birds"</b>.\n</p><p>The Orioles experienced their greatest success from 1966 to 1983, when they made six <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> appearances, winning three of them (<a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1970_World_Series" title="1970 World Series">1970</a>, <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Series" title="1983 World Series">1983</a>). This era of the club featured several future <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">Hall of Famers</a> who would later be inducted representing the Orioles, such as third baseman <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Robinson" title="Brooks Robinson">Brooks Robinson</a>, outfielder <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a>, starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jim_Palmer" title="Jim Palmer">Jim Palmer</a>, first baseman <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a>, shortstop <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a>, and manager <a href="/wiki/Earl_Weaver" title="Earl Weaver">Earl Weaver</a>. The Orioles have won a total of nine division championships (1969\xe2\x80\x931971, 1973\xe2\x80\x931974, 1979, 1983, 1997, 2014), six <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">pennants</a> (1966, 1969\xe2\x80\x931971, 1979, 1983), and three <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> berths (1996, 2012, 2016). \n</p><p>After suffering a stretch of 14 straight losing seasons from 1998 to 2011, the team qualified for the postseason three times under manager <a href="/wiki/Buck_Showalter" title="Buck Showalter">Buck Showalter</a> and general manager <a href="/wiki/Dan_Duquette" title="Dan Duquette">Dan Duquette</a>, including a division title and advancement to the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> for the first time in 17 years in <a href="/wiki/2014_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2014 Baltimore Orioles season">2014</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/2018_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2018 Baltimore Orioles season">2018</a> team finished with a franchise-worst record of 47-115, prompting the team to move on from Showalter and Duquette following the season\xe2\x80\x99s conclusion.\n</p><p>The Orioles are also well-known for their influential <a href="/wiki/Ballpark" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballpark">ballpark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a>, which opened in 1992 in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Baltimore" title="Downtown Baltimore">downtown Baltimore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li Famers</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Ford_C._Frick_Award_(broadcasters_only)"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ford C. Frick Award (broadcasters only)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Retired class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Season records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-56"><a href="#Individual_records_\xe2\x80\x93_batting"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Individual records \xe2\x80\x93 batting</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-57"><a tocsection-58"><a href="#Rivalry_with_the_Washington_Nationals"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalry with the Washington Nationals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-59"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-60"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-61"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-62"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Orioles" title="History of the Baltimore Orioles">History of the Baltimore Orioles</a></div>\n<p>The modern Orioles franchise can trace its roots back to the original Milwaukee Brewers of the <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">minor</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_League_(original)" class="mw-redirect" title="Western League (original)">Western League</a>, beginning in 1894, when the league reorganized. The Brewers were there when the WL renamed itself the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> in 1900.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milwaukee_Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Milwaukee Brewers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the end of the 1900 season, the American League removed itself from baseball\'s National Agreement (the formal understanding between the NL and the minor leagues). Two months later, the AL declared itself a competing major league. As a result of several franchise shifts, the Brewers were one of only two Western League teams that didn\'t fold, move or get kicked out of the league (the other being the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a>). In its first game in the American League, the team lost to the <a href="/wiki/1901_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1901 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> 14\xe2\x80\x9313 after blowing a nine-run lead in the 9th inning.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> To this day, it is a major league record for the biggest deficit overcome that late in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> During the first American League season in 1901, they finished last (eighth place) with a record of 48\xe2\x80\x9389. Its lone Major League season, the team played at <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Street_Grounds" title="Lloyd Street Grounds">Lloyd Street Grounds</a>, between 16th and 18th Streets in Milwaukee.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Louis_Browns">St. Louis Browns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: St. Louis Browns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Browns" title="History of the St. Louis Browns">History of the St. Louis Browns</a></div>\n<p>After one year in Milwaukee the club relocated to St Louis, and for a while enjoyed some success, especially in the 1920s behind Hall of Fame first baseman <a href="/wiki/George_Sisler" title="George Sisler">George Sisler</a>.  However, the team\'s fortunes declined from then on, as playing success and gate receipts instead went increasingly to the Browns\' own tenants at <a href="/wiki/Sportsman%27s_Park" title="Sportsman&#39;s Park">Sportsman\'s Park</a>, the National League <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a>.  During this period the Browns only won one pennant, in the 1944 season stocked with wartime replacement players, and lost to the Cardinals in the third and last World Series ever played entirely in one ballpark.  In 1953, with the Browns unable to afford even stadium upkeep, owner Bill Veeck sold Sportsman\'s Park to the Cards and attempted to move the club back to Milwaukee, but this was vetoed by the other Major League owners.  Instead, Veeck sold his franchise to a partnership of Baltimore businessmen.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Baltimore Orioles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orioles_Mascot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orioles_Mascot.jpg/220px-Orioles_Mascot.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orioles_Mascot.jpg/330px-Orioles_Mascot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orioles_Mascot.jpg/440px-Orioles_Mascot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orioles_Mascot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "Oriole Bird", which has been the official mascot figure since April 6, 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The Miles-Krieger (<a href="/wiki/Gunther_Brewing_Company" title="Gunther Brewing Company">Gunther Brewing Company</a>)-Hoffberger group renamed their new team the Baltimore Orioles soon after taking control of the franchise. The name has a rich history in Baltimore, having been used by a <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles_(19th_century)" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore Orioles (19th century)">National League team</a> in the 1890s. In 1901, Baltimore and John McGraw <sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>]] were awarded an expansion franchise in the growing American League, naming the team the Orioles. After a battle with Ban Johnson, the Head of the American League in 1902, McGraw took many of the top players including Walter Scott "Steve" Brodie, Dan McGann, Roger Bresnahan, and Joe McGinnity to the New York Giants.  As an affront to Johnson, McGraw kept the black and orange colors of the New York Giants, which San Francisco wears to this day. In 1903, the franchise -- the remaining players, assets and debts, the corporation -- was transferred to New York where they were nicknamed the Highlanders until circa 1912, by which time Yanks or Yankees had taken over as their popular moniker.  As a member of the high-minor league level <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles_(minor_league)" title="Baltimore Orioles (minor league)">Orioles</a> competed at what is now known as the AAA level from 1903 to 1953; the IL Orioles\' most famous player was a local Baltimore product, hard-hitting left-handed pitcher <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>. When Oriole Park burned down in 1944, the team moved to a temporary home, <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(Baltimore)" title="Memorial Stadium (Baltimore)">Municipal Stadium</a>, where they won the Junior World Series. Their large postseason crowds caught the attention of the major leagues, eventually leading to a new MLB franchise in Baltimore.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Seeds_of_success_.281954.E2.80.931959.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Seeds_of_success_(1954\xe2\x80\x931959)">Seeds of success (1954\xe2\x80\x931959)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Seeds of success (1954\xe2\x80\x931959)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After starting the <a href="/wiki/1954_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1954 Major League Baseball season">1954 campaign</a> with a two-game split against the <a href="/wiki/1954_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1954 Detroit Tigers season">Tigers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(Detroit)" title="Tiger Stadium (Detroit)">Detroit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1954_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1954 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> returned to Baltimore on April 15 to a welcoming parade that wound through the streets of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Baltimore" title="Downtown Baltimore">downtown</a>, with an estimated 350,000 spectators lining the route. In its first-ever home opener at <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Stadium_(Baltimore)" title="Memorial Stadium (Baltimore)">Memorial Stadium</a> later in the afternoon, they treated a sellout crowd of 46,354 to a 3\xe2\x80\x931 victory over the <a href="/wiki/1954_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1954 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a>. The remainder of the season would not be as pleasant, with the team enduring 100 losses while avoiding the AL cellar by only three games. With fellow investors both frustrated with his domination of the franchise\'s business operations and dissatisfied with yet another seventh-place finish, Clarence Miles resigned in early November 1955. Real estate developer <a href="/wiki/James_Keelty" title="James Keelty">James Keelty Jr.</a> succeeded him as president with investment banker <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Iglehart" title="Joseph Iglehart">Joseph Iglehart</a> the new board chairman.\n</p><p>The seeds of long-term success were planted on September 14, 1954, when the Orioles hired <a href="/wiki/Paul_Richards_(baseball)" title="Paul Richards (baseball)">Paul Richards</a> to become the ballclub\'s manager and general manager. He laid the foundation for what would years later be called the <i><b>Oriole Way</b></i>. The instruction of baseball fundamentals became uniform in every detail between all classes within the organization. Players were patiently refined until fundamentally sound instead of being hastily advanced to the next level.\n</p><p>For the remainder of the 1950s, the Orioles crawled up the standings, reaching as high as fifth place with a <a href="/wiki/1957_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1957 Baltimore Orioles season">76\xe2\x80\x9376</a> record in 1957. Richards succeeded in stocking the franchise with a plethora of young talent which included <a href="/wiki/Dave_Nicholson" title="Dave Nicholson">Dave Nicholson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Ward" title="Pete Ward">Pete Ward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Hansen_(baseball)" title="Ron Hansen (baseball)">Ron Hansen</a> (1960 AL <a href="/wiki/Rookie_of_the_Year_(award)" title="Rookie of the Year (award)">Rookie of the Year</a>), <a href="/wiki/Milt_Pappas" title="Milt Pappas">Milt Pappas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Adair" title="Jerry Adair">Jerry Adair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Barber" title="Steve Barber">Steve Barber</a> (20 wins in 1963), <a href="/wiki/Boog_Powell" title="Boog Powell">Boog Powell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_McNally" title="Dave McNally">Dave McNally</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Robinson" title="Brooks Robinson">Brooks Robinson</a>. Unfortunately, Richards also had the tendency to recklessly spend money on individuals with dubious baseball skills. This became a major problem as bidding wars between the ballclubs to land the best amateur players escalated signing bonuses.\n</p><p>The solution came on November 5, 1958, when <a href="/wiki/Lee_MacPhail" title="Lee MacPhail">Lee MacPhail</a> was appointed general manager, allowing Richards to focus on his managerial duties. MacPhail added much-needed discipline to the <a href="/wiki/Scout_(sport)" title="Scout (sport)">scouting</a> staff by establishing cross-checkers who thoroughly evaluated young hopefuls to determine whether they were worthy of being tendered a contract. He also accepted the title of president after Keelty resigned in mid-December 1959.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Pennant_contenders_.281960.E2.80.931965.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pennant_contenders_(1960\xe2\x80\x931965)">Pennant contenders (1960\xe2\x80\x931965)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pennant contenders (1960\xe2\x80\x931965)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>One month prior to the end of the 1961 season, Richards resigned as the team\'s skipper to become the general manager of the expansion <a href="/wiki/Houston_Colt_.45s" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Colt .45s">Houston Colt .45s</a>. A <a href="/wiki/1960_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1960 Major League Baseball season">year earlier</a>, he succeeded in establishing the <a href="/wiki/1960_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1960 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> as a legitimate contender when they stood atop the AL standings as late as early September before finishing in second place at 89\xe2\x80\x9365.\n</p><p>In 1964, the <a href="/wiki/1964_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1964 Baltimore Orioles season">Birds</a>, piloted by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Bauer" title="Hank Bauer">Hank Bauer</a> in his first year of managing the ballclub, were involved in a tight pennant race against the <a href="/wiki/1964_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1964 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> and <a href="/wiki/1964_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1964 Chicago White Sox season">White Sox</a>. They ended up in third place with a 97\xe2\x80\x9365 record, only two games out. It has been suggested that they would likely have advanced to the <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series" title="1964 World Series">Fall Classic</a> had it not been for a minor wrist injury that sidelined Powell for two weeks in late August.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, Robinson enjoyed a breakout season with a league-high 118 RBIs, and won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">AL Most Valuable Player Award</a>.\n</p><p>The television/radio network of <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>\' purchase of a majority stake in the Yankees on September 9 of that same year resulted in a change to the ownership situation in Baltimore. Iglehart, the Orioles\' largest shareholder at 32% and owner of a sizable amount of CBS stock, straightened out his conflict of interest issues on May 25, 1965, by selling his 64,000 shares in the ball-club to the <a href="/wiki/National_Bohemian" title="National Bohemian">National Brewing Company</a>, an original team investor which finally had controlling interest at 65%. Brewery president <a href="/wiki/Jerold_Hoffberger" title="Jerold Hoffberger">Jerold Hoffberger</a> became the Orioles\' new chairman of the board. Hoffberger\'s first action was installing <a href="/wiki/Frank_Cashen" title="Frank Cashen">Frank Cashen</a>, the Director of Advertising for the National Brewery, as Senior Vice President &amp; Chief Operating Officer for the Orioles.\n</p><p>With the benefit of a deep talent pool and superior scouts, the franchise continued to make improvements at the major league level. Three months before the start of the 1963 season, the <a href="/wiki/1963_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1963 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> stabilized its infield by acquiring <a href="/wiki/Luis_Aparicio" title="Luis Aparicio">Luis Aparicio</a> in a transaction that involved sending a trio of homegrown players (Hansen, Nicholson and Ward) to the White Sox. They also scoured the minor leagues for selections in the <a href="/wiki/Rule_5_draft" title="Rule 5 draft">Rule 5 draft</a> (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Blair_(baseball)" title="Paul Blair (baseball)">Paul Blair</a> from the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">Mets</a> in 1962, <a href="/wiki/Moe_Drabowsky" title="Moe Drabowsky">Moe Drabowsky</a> from the Cardinals in 1965) and claims off waivers (<a href="/wiki/Curt_Blefary" title="Curt Blefary">Curt Blefary</a>, 1965 <a href="/wiki/AL_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="AL Rookie of the Year">AL Rookie of the Year</a>, from the Yankees in 1963).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Milt_Pappas_for_Frank_Robinson">Milt Pappas for Frank Robinson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Milt Pappas for Frank Robinson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg/220px-Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg" width="220" height="354" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg/330px-Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg/440px-Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1243" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Tobias_Mendez.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a> statue by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tobias_Mendez" title="Antonio Tobias Mendez">Antonio Tobias Mendez</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>On December 9, 1965, the Orioles traded pitcher <a href="/wiki/Milt_Pappas" title="Milt Pappas">Milt Pappas</a> (and several others) to the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> in exchange for slugging outfielder <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a>. The following year, Robinson won the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Most_Valuable_Player" class="mw-redirect" title="American League Most Valuable Player">American League Most Valuable Player</a> award, thus becoming the first (and so far only) man to win the MVP in each league (Robinson won the NL MVP in 1961, leading the Reds to the pennant). In addition to winning the 1966 MVP, Robinson also won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a> (leading the American League in batting average, home runs, and runs batted in), a feat also achieved the following season by <a href="/wiki/1962_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1962 Boston Red Sox season">Boston\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Carl_Yastrzemski" title="Carl Yastrzemski">Carl Yastrzemski</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1966_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1966 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> won their first-ever American League championship in 1966, and in a major upset, swept the <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">World Series</a> by out-dueling the defending World Champion <a href="/wiki/1966_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1966 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, whose pitching staff was led by aces <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Koufax" title="Sandy Koufax">Sandy Koufax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a>. The only home run ball ever hit completely out of Memorial Stadium was slugged by Robinson on Mother\'s Day in 1966, off <a href="/wiki/1966_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1966 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Luis_Tiant" title="Luis Tiant">Luis Tiant</a>. It cleared the left field single-deck portion of the grandstand. A flag was later erected near the spot the ball cleared the back wall, with simply the word "HERE" upon it. The flag is now in the Baltimore Orioles Museum.\n</p><p>Pappas went 30\xe2\x80\x9329 in a little over two years with the Reds before being traded. Although he would go on to have back-to-back 17-win seasons for the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> in 1971 and 1972, including a no-hitter in the latter season, this did not help the <a href="/wiki/1970_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1970 Cincinnati Reds season">Reds</a>, who ended up losing the <a href="/wiki/1970_World_Series" title="1970 World Series">1970 World Series</a> to Robinson and the Orioles. This trade has become renowned as one of the most lopsided in baseball history, including a mention by <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a> in her opening soliloquy in the 1988 film <i><a href="/wiki/Bull_Durham" title="Bull Durham">Bull Durham</a></i>: "Bad trades are a part of baseball. I mean, who can forget Frank Robinson for Milt Pappas?"<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Glory_years_.281966.E2.80.931983.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Glory_years_(1966\xe2\x80\x931983)">Glory years (1966\xe2\x80\x931983)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Glory years (1966\xe2\x80\x931983)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the 1960s, the Orioles farm system produced an especially large number of high-quality players and coaches and laid the foundation for two decades of on-field success. This period included eighteen consecutive winning seasons (1968\xe2\x80\x931985) -- a run of success that saw the Orioles become the envy of the league, and the winningest team in baseball.\n</p><p>During this period, the Orioles played baseball the "Oriole Way", an organizational ethic best described by longtime farm hand and coach <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Sr." title="Cal Ripken Sr.">Cal Ripken Sr.</a>\'s phrase "perfect practice makes perfect!" The Oriole Way was a belief that hard work, professionalism, and a strong understanding of fundamentals were the keys to success at the major league level. It was based on the belief that if every coach, at every level, taught the game the same way, the organization could produce "replacement parts" that could be substituted seamlessly into the big league club with little or no adjustment. Elaborations on the Oriole way include pitching coach and manager Ray Miller\'s maxim "Work fast, change speeds, and throw strikes" and manager Earl Weaver\'s maxim "Pitching, defense and three-run homers."\n"\nThe "Oriole Way" began flourishing in 1966 after the Robinson-for-Pappas deal, as Robinson won the "Triple Crown Award". His Orioles would easily sweep the <a href="/wiki/1966_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1966 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966 World Series</a>. After a mediocre <a href="/wiki/1967_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1967 Baltimore Orioles season">1967 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Bauer" title="Hank Bauer">Hank Bauer</a> would be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Earl_Weaver" title="Earl Weaver">Earl Weaver</a> halfway into 1968. The <a href="/wiki/1968_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1968 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> would finish second in the American League. This would only be a prelude to 1969, when the <a href="/wiki/1969_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1969 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> won 109&#160;games and easily won the newly created <a href="/wiki/American_League_East" title="American League East">American League East</a> division title. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Cuellar" title="Mike Cuellar">Mike Cuellar</a> shared the <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> with Detroit\'s <a href="/wiki/Denny_McLain" title="Denny McLain">Denny McLain</a>. After sweeping <a href="/wiki/1969_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1969 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1969_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1969 American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a>, Baltimore was shocked by losing to the <a href="/wiki/1969_New_York_Mets_season" title="1969 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> in a five-game <a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">World Series</a>. The next year, <a href="/wiki/Boog_Powell" title="Boog Powell">Boog Powell</a> won the MVP and the Orioles won another 108&#160;games. After sweeping the <a href="/wiki/1970_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1970 Minnesota Twins season">Twins</a> once again in the <a href="/wiki/1970_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1970 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, the Orioles won the <a href="/wiki/1970_World_Series" title="1970 World Series">1970 World Series</a> by defeating the <a href="/wiki/1970_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1970 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Big_Red_Machine" title="Big Red Machine">Big Red Machine</a> in five games.\n</p><p>In 1971, the <a href="/wiki/1971_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1971 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> won another division title thanks to four 20-game winners on their pitching staff (Cuellar, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Palmer" title="Jim Palmer">Jim Palmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pat_Dobson" title="Pat Dobson">Pat Dobson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dave_McNally" title="Dave McNally">Dave McNally</a>). After defeating the young <a href="/wiki/1971_Oakland_Athletics_season" title="1971 Oakland Athletics season">Oakland A\'s</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1971_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1971 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, the Orioles would lose a heartbreaking seven-game <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series" title="1971 World Series">World Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1971_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1971 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1972_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1972 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> would miss the playoffs in 1972, but rebounded to win the division in 1973 and 1974. Each time, they would lose to Oakland in the ALCS. During this stretch, the Orioles began to phase out their veteran infield by replacing <a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnson" title="Davey Johnson">Davey Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Robinson" title="Brooks Robinson">Brooks Robinson</a> with younger stars <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Grich" title="Bobby Grich">Bobby Grich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doug_DeCinces" title="Doug DeCinces">Doug DeCinces</a>, respectively. Johnson would be dealt along with <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Oates" title="Johnny Oates">Johnny Oates</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> for catcher and 1971 <a href="/wiki/National_League_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="National League Rookie of the Year">National League Rookie of the Year</a> <a href="/wiki/Earl_Williams_(1970s_catcher)" title="Earl Williams (1970s catcher)">Earl Williams</a>. Although Williams had hit 63 home runs in two seasons with Atlanta, he would only hit 36 homers in two seasons with the Orioles.\n</p><p>In 1975, the Birds acquired slugger <a href="/wiki/Lee_May" title="Lee May">Lee May</a> in a trade with Houston, and traded <a href="/wiki/Dave_McNally" title="Dave McNally">Dave McNally</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rich_Coggins" title="Rich Coggins">Rich Coggins</a> and minor-league pitcher Bill Kirkpatrick to <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal</a> for star outfielder <a href="/wiki/Ken_Singleton" title="Ken Singleton">Ken Singleton</a>, and future 20-game winner <a href="/wiki/Mike_Torrez" title="Mike Torrez">Mike Torrez</a>. Jim Palmer won the Cy Young Award, but the <a href="/wiki/1975_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1975 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> lost the division title to the <a href="/wiki/1975_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1975 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> and their mega-rookies <a href="/wiki/Fred_Lynn" title="Fred Lynn">Fred Lynn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rice" title="Jim Rice">Jim Rice</a>. The 1976 season brought <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Holtzman" title="Ken Holtzman">Ken Holtzman</a> from a trade with Oakland, but the <a href="/wiki/1976_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1976 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> only won 88&#160;games. It was this season when the Orioles made a trade that brought them players such as <a href="/wiki/Tippy_Martinez" title="Tippy Martinez">Tippy Martinez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Dempsey" title="Rick Dempsey">Rick Dempsey</a>. This young foundation, along with the departures of the unhappy Jackson and Holtzman, would create the basis for 1977. The <a href="/wiki/1977_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1977 Baltimore Orioles season">"No Name Orioles"</a>, along with Rookie of the Year <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a>, won 97&#160;games and finished tied for second place with <a href="/wiki/1977_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1977 Boston Red Sox season">Boston</a>. After finishing fourth in 1978, the <a href="/wiki/1979_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1979 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> finally won the division in 1979 thanks to strong play from Ken Singleton and Cy Young winner <a href="/wiki/Mike_Flanagan_(baseball)" title="Mike Flanagan (baseball)">Mike Flanagan</a>. The Orioles defeated the <a href="/wiki/1979_California_Angels_season" title="1979 California Angels season">Angels</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1979_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1979 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, but lost to <a href="/wiki/1979_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1979 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh</a> in another <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Series" title="1979 World Series">stunning World Series</a>. This started a short period of heartbreak for Baltimore that would nevertheless culminate in a championship.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg/180px-Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg" width="180" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg/270px-Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg/360px-Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1234" data-file-height="1544" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Stone_interviews_Mike_Mullen_CROP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1980_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1980 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> won 100&#160;games in 1980 thanks to Cy Young winner <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a> who went 25\xe2\x80\x937 (.781) while leading the league in wins (a franchise record) and win-loss percentage, but the <a href="/wiki/1980_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1980 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> won 103&#160;games. Although <a href="/wiki/1981_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1981 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore</a> had the best overall record in the AL East in 1981, they finished second in each half. As a result, they were out of the playoffs due to the postseason structure that year because of the <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">strike</a>. The 1982 campaign saw Baltimore eliminated on the final weekend of the season by the <a href="/wiki/1982_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="1982 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a>. In an unforgettable scene, despite the season-ending loss eliminating them from the playoffs, fans stayed to honor the retiring <a href="/wiki/Earl_Weaver" title="Earl Weaver">Earl Weaver</a>, who would be succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Altobelli" title="Joe Altobelli">Joe Altobelli</a>. In 1983, Altobelli would lead the Orioles to 98 wins and a division title thanks to MVP <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1983_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1983 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/1983_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1983 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1983_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1983 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> thanks to a 10th-inning homer by <a href="/wiki/Tito_Landrum" title="Tito Landrum">Tito Landrum</a> in the deciding game. The Orioles won the <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Series" title="1983 World Series">World Series</a> in five games by defeating the <a href="/wiki/1983_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="1983 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a>.\n</p><p>During their most productive years and only World Series championships thus far, the Orioles saw three of its players named MVP: Frank Robinson in 1966; Boog Powell in 1970; and Cal Ripken Jr. in 1983. Additionally, Brooks Robinson was named Most Valuable Player in 1964, just two years before the 1966\xe2\x80\x931983 golden era began. The pitching staff was phenomenal, with four pitchers winning six <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a> (Mike Cuellar in 1969; Jim Palmer in 1973, 1975, and 1976; Mike Flanagan in 1979; and Steve Stone in 1980). In 1971, the team\'s four starting pitchers, McNally, Cuellar, Palmer, and Pat Dobson, all won 20&#160;games, a feat that has not been replicated. In that year, the Birds went on to post a 101\xe2\x80\x9361 record for their third-straight AL East title.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Also during this stretch three players were named <a href="/wiki/American_League_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="American League Rookie of the Year">rookies of the year</a>: <a href="/wiki/Al_Bumbry" title="Al Bumbry">Al Bumbry</a> (1973); Eddie Murray (1977); and Cal Ripken Jr. (1982). One might date the glory years of the Orioles dating back to 1964, which would include two third-place seasons, 1964\xe2\x80\x9365, in which the Orioles won 97 and 94&#160;games, respectively, and a year in which third-baseman Brooks Robinson won his <a href="/wiki/Most_Valuable_Player_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player Award</a> (1964). The glory years of the Orioles effectively ended when the <a href="/wiki/1984_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1984 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a>, a divisional rival at the time, went 35\xe2\x80\x935 to open the 1984 season on the way to winning the World Series, in which Hall-of-Fame pitcher Jim Palmer retired during the 1984 season.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Final_seasons_at_Memorial_Stadium_.281984.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_seasons_at_Memorial_Stadium_(1984\xe2\x80\x931991)">Final seasons at Memorial Stadium (1984\xe2\x80\x931991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Final seasons at Memorial Stadium (1984\xe2\x80\x931991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg/250px-Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg" width="250" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg/375px-Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg/500px-Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1771" data-file-height="1210" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Memorial_Stadium_1991.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Orioles hosting one of the final games at Memorial Stadium in 1991.</div></div></div>\n<p>After winning the <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Series" title="1983 World Series">1983 World Series</a>, the Orioles spent the next five years in steady decline, finishing 1986 in last place for the first time since the franchise moved to Baltimore. The <a href="/wiki/1988_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1988 Baltimore Orioles season">team</a> hit bottom in 1988 when it started the season 0\xe2\x80\x9321, en route to 107 losses and the worst record in the majors that year. The "Why Not?" Orioles surprised the baseball world the following year by spending most of the summer in first place until September when the <a href="/wiki/1989_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="1989 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> overtook them and seized the AL East title on the final weekend of the regular season. The next two years were spent below the .500 mark, highlighted only by Cal Ripken Jr. winning his second <a href="/wiki/AL_MVP_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="AL MVP Award">AL MVP Award</a> in 1991. The <a href="/wiki/1991_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1991 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> said goodbye to Memorial Stadium, the team\'s home for 38&#160;years, at the end of the 1991 campaign.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png/150px-Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png" width="150" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png/225px-Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png/300px-Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles_wordmark_1988_to_1994.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Orioles wordmark (1988\xe2\x80\x931994)</div></div></div>\n<h4><span id="Camden_Yards_opens_.281992.E2.80.931993.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Camden_Yards_opens_(1992\xe2\x80\x931993)">Camden Yards opens (1992\xe2\x80\x931993)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Camden Yards opens (1992\xe2\x80\x931993)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/1992_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1992 Baltimore Orioles season">1992 Baltimore Orioles season</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1993 Baltimore Orioles season">1993 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>Opening to much fanfare in 1992, <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a> was an instant success, spawning other retro-designed major league ballparks within the next two decades. The stadium became the site of the <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="1993 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">1993 All-Star Game</a>. The Orioles returned to contention in those first two seasons at Camden Yards, only to finish in third place both times.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Angelos_takes_over">Angelos takes over</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Angelos takes over">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>Also in 1993, with then-owner <a href="/wiki/Eli_Jacobs" title="Eli Jacobs">Eli Jacobs</a> forced to divest himself of the franchise, Baltimore-based attorney <a href="/wiki/Peter_Angelos" title="Peter Angelos">Peter Angelos</a>, along with the ownership syndicate he headed, was awarded the Orioles in <a href="/wiki/United_States_bankruptcy_court" title="United States bankruptcy court">bankruptcy court</a> in New York City, returning the team to local ownership for the first time since 1979.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Strike_year_.281994.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Strike_year_(1994)">Strike year (1994)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Strike year (1994)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1994_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1994 Baltimore Orioles season">1994 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>After the 1993 season, the Orioles acquired first baseman <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>. The Orioles, who spent all of 1994 chasing the <a href="/wiki/1994_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1994 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a>, occupied second place in the new five-team AL East when the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players strike</a>, which began on August 11, forced the eventual cancellation of the season.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Ripken_breaks_the_streak_.281995.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ripken_breaks_the_streak_(1995)">Ripken breaks the streak (1995)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ripken breaks the streak (1995)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg/250px-2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg/375px-2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="376" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2131_on_the_warehouse_wall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The numbers on the Orioles\' warehouse changed from 2130 to 2131 to celebrate Cal Ripken Jr. passing Lou Gehrig\'s consecutive games played streak.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1995_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1995 Baltimore Orioles season">1995 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The labor impasse would continue into the spring of 1995. Almost all of the major league clubs held spring training using <a href="/wiki/Strikebreaker" title="Strikebreaker">replacement players</a>, with the intention of beginning the <a href="/wiki/1995_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1995 Major League Baseball season">season</a> with them. The Orioles, whose owner was a labor union lawyer, were the lone dissenters against creating an ersatz team, choosing instead to sit out spring training and possibly the entire season. Had they fielded a substitute team, <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a>\'s consecutive games streak would have been jeopardized. The replacements questions became moot when the strike was finally settled.\n</p><p>The Ripken countdown resumed once the season began. Ripken finally broke <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>\'s consecutive games streak of 2,130&#160;games in a nationally televised game on September 6. This was later voted the all-time baseball moment of the 20th century by fans from around the country in 1999. Ripken finished his streak with 2,632 straight games, finally sitting on September 20, 1998, the <a href="/wiki/1998_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1998 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> final home game of the season against the <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> at Camden Yards.\n</p><p>The Orioles finished two games under .500 (71\xe2\x80\x9373) in third place in <a href="/wiki/Phil_Regan_(baseball)" title="Phil Regan (baseball)">Phil Regan</a>\'s only season of managing the ballclub.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Playoff_years_.281996.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Playoff_years_(1996\xe2\x80\x931997)">Playoff years (1996\xe2\x80\x931997)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Playoff years (1996\xe2\x80\x931997)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1996_season">1996 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1996 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1996_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1996 Baltimore Orioles season">1996 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>Before the 1996 season, Angelos hired <a href="/wiki/Pat_Gillick" title="Pat Gillick">Pat Gillick</a> as general manager. Given the green light to spend heavily on established talent, Gillick signed several premium players like <a href="/wiki/B._J._Surhoff" title="B. J. Surhoff">B. J. Surhoff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Myers" title="Randy Myers">Randy Myers</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Wells" title="David Wells">David Wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Alomar" title="Roberto Alomar">Roberto Alomar</a>. Under new manager <a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnson" title="Davey Johnson">Davey Johnson</a> and on the strength of a then-major league record 257 home runs in a single season, the Orioles returned to the playoffs after a 12-year absence by clinching the AL wild card berth. Alomar set off a firestorm in September when he spat into home plate umpire <a href="/wiki/John_Hirschbeck" title="John Hirschbeck">John Hirschbeck</a>\'s face during an argument in Toronto. He was later suspended for the first five games of the 1997 season, even though most wanted him banned from the postseason. After dethroning the defending American League champion <a href="/wiki/1996_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1996 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a> 3\xe2\x80\x931 in the <a href="/wiki/1996_American_League_Division_Series" title="1996 American League Division Series">Division Series</a>, the Orioles fell to the <a href="/wiki/1996_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1996 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> 4\xe2\x80\x931 in an <a href="/wiki/1996_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1996 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> notable for right field umpire <a href="/wiki/Rich_Garcia" title="Rich Garcia">Rich Garcia</a>\'s failure to call fan interference in the first game of the series, when 12-year-old Yankee fan <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Maier" title="Jeffrey Maier">Jeffrey Maier</a> reached over the outfield wall to catch an in-play ball, which was scored as a home run for <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a>, tying the game at 4\xe2\x80\x934 in the eighth inning. Absent Maier\'s interference, it appeared as if the ball might have been off the wall or caught by right fielder <a href="/wiki/Tony_Tarasco" title="Tony Tarasco">Tony Tarasco</a>. The Yankees went on to win the game in extra innings on an ensuing walk-off home run by Bernie Williams.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1997_season">1997 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1997 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1997_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1997 Baltimore Orioles season">1997 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The Orioles went "wire-to-wire" (first place from start to finish) in winning the AL East title in 1997. After eliminating the <a href="/wiki/1997_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="1997 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a> 3\xe2\x80\x931 in the <a href="/wiki/1997_American_League_Division_Series" title="1997 American League Division Series">Division Series</a>, the team lost again in the <a href="/wiki/1997_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1997 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, this time to the underdog <a href="/wiki/1997_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1997 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> 4\xe2\x80\x932, with each Oriole loss by only a run. Johnson resigned as manager after the season, largely due to a spat with Angelos concerning Alomar\'s fine for missing a team function being donated to Johnson\'s wife\'s charity.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Pitching coach <a href="/wiki/Ray_Miller_(baseball_manager)" title="Ray Miller (baseball manager)">Ray Miller</a> replaced Johnson.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Beginning_of_a_downturn_.281998.E2.80.932001.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning_of_a_downturn_(1998\xe2\x80\x932001)">Beginning of a downturn (1998\xe2\x80\x932001)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Beginning of a downturn (1998\xe2\x80\x932001)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1998_season">1998 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1998 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1998_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1998 Baltimore Orioles season">1998 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>With Miller at the helm, the Orioles found themselves not only out of the playoffs, but also with a losing season. When Gillick\'s contract expired in 1998, it was not renewed. Angelos brought in <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wren" title="Frank Wren">Frank Wren</a> to take over as GM. The Orioles added volatile slugger <a href="/wiki/Albert_Belle" title="Albert Belle">Albert Belle</a>, but the team\'s woes continued in the 1999 season, with stars like <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Alomar" title="Roberto Alomar">Roberto Alomar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Davis_(baseball)" title="Eric Davis (baseball)">Eric Davis</a> leaving in free agency. After a second straight losing season, Angelos fired both Miller and Wren. He named <a href="/wiki/Syd_Thrift" title="Syd Thrift">Syd Thrift</a> the new GM and brought in former Cleveland manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hargrove" title="Mike Hargrove">Mike Hargrove</a>.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1999_season">1999 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1999 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1999_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1999 Baltimore Orioles season">1999 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Baltimore_Orioles.svg/150px-Baltimore_Orioles.svg.png" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Baltimore_Orioles.svg/225px-Baltimore_Orioles.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Baltimore_Orioles.svg/300px-Baltimore_Orioles.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo (1999\xe2\x80\x932008).</div></div></div><p>In a rare event on March 28, 1999, the Orioles staged an <a href="/wiki/1999_Baltimore_Orioles_%E2%80%93_Cuban_national_baseball_team_exhibition_series" title="1999 Baltimore Orioles \xe2\x80\x93 Cuban national baseball team exhibition series">exhibition series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Cuba_national_baseball_team" title="Cuba national baseball team">Cuban national team</a> in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>. The Orioles won the game 3\xe2\x80\x932 in 11 innings. They were the first Major League team to play in Cuba since 1959, when the <a href="/wiki/1959_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1959 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> faced the <a href="/wiki/1959_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1959 Baltimore Orioles season">Orioles</a> in an exhibition. The Cuban team visited Baltimore in May 1999. Cuba won the second game 10\xe2\x80\x936.\n</p><h5><span id="2000.E2.80.932001_seasons"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\xe2\x80\x932001_seasons">2000\xe2\x80\x932001 seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2000\xe2\x80\x932001 seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2000_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2000 Baltimore Orioles season">2000 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>Cal Ripken Jr. achieved his 3000th hit early in the season. A fire sale occurred late in the season, where the Orioles traded away many veterans for unproven young players and minor league prospects. The Orioles called up many of their AAA players to finish the season. The only acquired player that would have a long-term career with the organization was <a href="/wiki/Melvin_Mora" title="Melvin Mora">Melvin Mora</a>.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2001_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2001 Baltimore Orioles season">2001 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>This was Cal Ripken Jr.\'s final season. His number (8) was retired in a ceremony before the final home game of the season.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Post-Ripken_era_and_downfall_.282002-2011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Ripken_era_and_downfall_(2002-2011)">Post-Ripken era and downfall (2002-2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Post-Ripken era and downfall (2002-2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2002-2004_seasons">2002-2004 seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2002-2004 seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg/220px-Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg.png" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg/330px-Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg/440px-Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="137" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Orioles_Script.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This version of the script logo has been on the front of the home jerseys since 2004.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2002_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2002 Baltimore Orioles season">2002 Baltimore Orioles season</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2003 Baltimore Orioles season">2003 Baltimore Orioles season</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2004_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2004 Baltimore Orioles season">2004 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The team\xe2\x80\x99s first year without Ripken saw the team with a record of 63-63 at the conclusion of play on August 23, but then proceed to lose 32 of its last 36 games of the season, including their final 12 in a row to finish the season 67-95. In an effort to right the Orioles\' sinking ship, changes began to sweep through the organization in 2003. General manager <a href="/wiki/Syd_Thrift" title="Syd Thrift">Syd Thrift</a> was fired and to replace him, the Orioles hired <a href="/wiki/Jim_Beattie_(baseball)" title="Jim Beattie (baseball)">Jim Beattie</a> as executive vice-president and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Flanagan_(baseball)" title="Mike Flanagan (baseball)">Mike Flanagan</a> as the vice president of baseball operations. After another losing season, manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hargrove" title="Mike Hargrove">Mike Hargrove</a> was not retained and Yankees coach <a href="/wiki/Lee_Mazzilli" title="Lee Mazzilli">Lee Mazzilli</a> was brought in as the new manager. The team signed powerful hitters in SS <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Tejada" title="Miguel Tejada">Miguel Tejada</a>, C <a href="/wiki/Javy_L%C3%B3pez" title="Javy L\xc3\xb3pez">Javy L\xc3\xb3pez</a>, and former Oriole 1B <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a>. The following season, the Orioles traded for OF <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a>.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_season">2005 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2005 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/250px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/375px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg/500px-CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CamdenYards_2005-05-08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Orioles taking on the Kansas City Royals at home in 2005.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2005_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2005 Baltimore Orioles season">2005 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The team got hot early in 2005 and jumped out in front of the AL East division, holding onto first place for 62 straight days. However, turmoil on and off the field began to take its toll as the Orioles started struggling around the All-Star break, dropping them close to the surging <a href="/wiki/2005_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2005 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> and <a href="/wiki/2005_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2005 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a>. Injuries to Lopez, Sosa, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Matos" title="Luis Matos">Luis Matos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Roberts_(baseball)" title="Brian Roberts (baseball)">Brian Roberts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Bigbie" title="Larry Bigbie">Larry Bigbie</a> came within weeks of each other, and the team grew increasingly dissatisfied with the "band-aid" moves of the front office and manager Mazzilli to help them through this period of struggle. Various minor league players such as Single-A Frederick OF <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Fiorentino" title="Jeff Fiorentino">Jeff Fiorentino</a> were brought up in place of more experienced players such as OF <a href="/wiki/David_Newhan" title="David Newhan">David Newhan</a>, who had batted .311 the previous season.\n</p><p>After starting the season 42\xe2\x80\x9328 (.600), the Orioles finished the season with a stretch of 32\xe2\x80\x9360 (.348), ending at 74\xe2\x80\x9388 (.457). Only the <a href="/wiki/2005_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="2005 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a> (.346) had a worse winning percentage for the season than did the Orioles for the final 92&#160;games. The club\'s major off-season acquisition, <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a>, posted his worst performance in a decade, with 14 home runs and a .221 batting average. The Orioles did not attempt to re-sign him. The Orioles also allowed Palmeiro to file for free agency and publicly stated they would not re-sign him. On August 25, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Ponson" title="Sidney Ponson">Sidney Ponson</a> was arrested for DUI, and on September 1, the Orioles moved to void his contract (on a morals clause) and released him. The <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">Major League Baseball Players Association</a> filed a grievance on Ponson\'s behalf and the case was sent to arbitration and was eventually resolved.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_season">2006 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2006 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2006 Baltimore Orioles season">2006 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">2006 World Baseball Classic</a>, the Orioles contributed more players than any other major league team, with eleven players suiting up for their home nations. <a href="/wiki/%C3%89rik_B%C3%A9dard" title="\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard">\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Loewen" title="Adam Loewen">Adam Loewen</a> pitched for <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_baseball_team" title="Canada national baseball team">Canada</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_L%C3%B3pez_(baseball)" title="Rodrigo L\xc3\xb3pez (baseball)">Rodrigo L\xc3\xb3pez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ger%C3%B3nimo_Gil" title="Ger\xc3\xb3nimo Gil">Ger\xc3\xb3nimo Gil</a> (released before the season began by the club) played for <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_baseball_team" title="Mexico national baseball team">Mexico</a>; <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Cabrera" title="Daniel Cabrera">Daniel Cabrera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Tejada" title="Miguel Tejada">Miguel Tejada</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_national_baseball_team" title="Dominican Republic national baseball team">Dominican Republic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Javy_L%C3%B3pez" title="Javy L\xc3\xb3pez">Javy L\xc3\xb3pez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Matos" title="Luis Matos">Luis Matos</a> for <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_national_baseball_team" title="Puerto Rico national baseball team">Puerto Rico</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Chen" title="Bruce Chen">Bruce Chen</a> for <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_baseball_team" title="Panama national baseball team">Panama</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Ram\xc3\xb3n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a> for <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_national_baseball_team" title="Venezuela national baseball team">Venezuela</a>; and <a href="/wiki/John_Stephens_(baseball)" title="John Stephens (baseball)">John Stephens</a> for <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_baseball_team" title="Australia national baseball team">Australia</a>. The Orioles finished the 2006 season with a record of 70 wins and 92 losses, 27&#160;games behind the AL East-leading <a href="/wiki/2006_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2006 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a>.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_season">2007 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2007 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2007_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2007 Baltimore Orioles season">2007 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>On June 18, the Orioles fired <a href="/wiki/Sam_Perlozzo" title="Sam Perlozzo">Sam Perlozzo</a> after losing eight straight games. He was replaced on interim basis by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Trembley" title="Dave Trembley">Dave Trembley</a>. On June 22, Miguel Tejada\'s consecutive-games streak came to an end due to an injury, the fifth-longest streak in major league history. <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Huff" title="Aubrey Huff">Aubrey Huff</a> became the first Oriole to hit for the cycle at home, on June 29 against the Angels. On July 7, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89rik_B%C3%A9dard" title="\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard">\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard</a> struck out 15 batters in a game against the <a href="/wiki/2007_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2007 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> to tie a franchise record held by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Mussina" title="Mike Mussina">Mike Mussina</a>. On July 31, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Andy_MacPhail" title="Andy MacPhail">Andy MacPhail</a> named Dave Trembley as the Orioles manager through the remainder of the 2007 season, and advised him to "Keep up the good work."<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Facing the <a href="/wiki/2007_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2007 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> in a doubleheader at Camden Yards on August 22, the Orioles surrendered 30 runs in the first game, a modern-era record for a single game, in a 30\xe2\x80\x933 defeat. The Orioles led the game 3\xe2\x80\x930 after three innings of play. Sixteen of Texas\' thirty runs were scored in the final two innings. The Orioles would also fall in the nightcap, 9\xe2\x80\x937.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_season">2008 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2008 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2008 Baltimore Orioles season">2008 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The Orioles began the 2008 season in a rebuilding mode under President of Baseball Operations <a href="/wiki/Andy_MacPhail" title="Andy MacPhail">Andy MacPhail</a>. The Orioles traded away star players <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Tejada" title="Miguel Tejada">Miguel Tejada</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Astros</a> and ace <a href="/wiki/%C3%89rik_B%C3%A9dard" title="\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard">\xc3\x89rik B\xc3\xa9dard</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> for prized prospect <a href="/wiki/Adam_Jones_(baseball)" title="Adam Jones (baseball)">Adam Jones</a>, lefty reliever <a href="/wiki/George_Sherrill" title="George Sherrill">George Sherrill</a>, and minor league pitchers <a href="/wiki/Kam_Mickolio" title="Kam Mickolio">Kam Mickolio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Tillman" title="Chris Tillman">Chris Tillman</a>, and Tony Butler. The Orioles started off the first couple weeks of the season near the top of their division as players such as <a href="/wiki/Nick_Markakis" title="Nick Markakis">Nick Markakis</a> and newcomer <a href="/wiki/Luke_Scott" title="Luke Scott">Luke Scott</a> led the team offensively. Although the Orioles hovered around .500 for much of the season, they had fallen back by September and were over 20&#160;games behind the first place <a href="/wiki/2008_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2008 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a>. They finished the season losing 11 of their final 12&#160;games and 28 of their final 34. The team finished last for the first time since their 1988 season.\n</p><p>After the season ended, the Orioles showcased altered uniforms, with a circular \'Maryland\' patch added to the left-hand sleeve of all jerseys and the grey road jerseys displaying "Baltimore" across the chest for the first time in a quarter-century; this reflected the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>, because ever since the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">Washington Senators</a> had departed for Texas in 1972, the Orioles had claimed to represent the Baltimore-Washington metro area.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_season">2009 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2009 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2009_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2009 Baltimore Orioles season">2009 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nick_Markakis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Nick_Markakis.jpg/220px-Nick_Markakis.jpg" width="220" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Nick_Markakis.jpg/330px-Nick_Markakis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Nick_Markakis.jpg/440px-Nick_Markakis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2119" data-file-height="2454" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nick_Markakis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adam Jones and Nick Markakis, Orioles v.
