Tampa Bay Rays, Camden Yards, April 12, 2009.</div></div></div>\n<p>On June 30, the Orioles rallied to score 10 runs against <a href="/wiki/2009_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2009 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> after facing a 10\xe2\x80\x931 deficit in the 7th inning, winning the game by 11\xe2\x80\x9310, setting a Major League Baseball record for the largest comeback by a last-place team over a first-place team.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> However, the team finished the 2009 season with 64 wins and 98 losses, making it the worst record in the 2009 American League season. Despite this, Manager <a href="/wiki/Dave_Trembley" title="Dave Trembley">Dave Trembley</a> was re-hired for the 2010 season.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Centerfielder Adam Jones was named to the <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2009 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2009 All Star team</a>, and awarded a Gold Glove award for his defensive play.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_season">2010 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2010 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2010 Baltimore Orioles season">2010 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>On April 12, the team set a club record for the lowest paid attendance in Camden Yards history, only 9,129 attended the game versus the <a href="/wiki/2010_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2010 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The Orioles then went 2\xe2\x80\x9316 to begin the <a href="/wiki/2010_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2010 Major League Baseball season">season</a>, last in the league by quite a margin.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 4, with an 8 game losing streak and the worst record in the league at 15\xe2\x80\x9339, the Orioles replaced <a href="/wiki/Dave_Trembley" title="Dave Trembley">Dave Trembley</a> as manager with third base coach <a href="/wiki/Juan_Samuel" title="Juan Samuel">Juan Samuel</a> as interim manager.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> They did well at first, but then they started losing again, going 17\xe2\x80\x9334 under Samuel.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebowitz2011_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebowitz2011-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The Orioles hired <a href="/wiki/Buck_Showalter" title="Buck Showalter">Buck Showalter</a> on July 29 to be the full-time manager.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He was introduced on August 2 and made his debut on August 3, after the Orioles fired Samuel. Showalter\'s arrival produced, or coincided with, a turnaround; the Birds went 34\xe2\x80\x9323 under Showalter to finish 66-96.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebowitz2011_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebowitz2011-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG/220px-Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG/330px-Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG/440px-Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orioles_Win_May_13_2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Orioles celebrate a 6\xe2\x80\x935 victory over the Mariners at Camden Yards on May 13, 2010.</div></div></div>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_season">2011 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2011 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2011 Baltimore Orioles season">2011 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>On February 4, 2011, the Orioles signed free agent <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">Vladimir Guerrero</a> to be the team\'s designated hitter. Playing for the Texas Rangers during the 2010 season, Guerrero had hit 29 home runs, with a .300 batting average. (His career batting average was .320 with 436 home runs.)\n</p><p>The Orioles 2011 record was 69\xe2\x80\x9393, the 14th consecutive losing season for the franchise dating back to 1998. The highlight of the season was their final game on September 28, when they defeated the <a href="/wiki/2011_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2011 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> 4\xe2\x80\x933 thanks to 9th inning heroics by <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Reimold" title="Nolan Reimold">Nolan Reimold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Andino" title="Robert Andino">Robert Andino</a>. The Orioles victory prevented the Red Sox from earning the wild card berth as part of "<a href="/wiki/Game_162" class="mw-redirect" title="Game 162">Game 162</a>", one of the most dramatic nights in Major League Baseball history. On November 8, the Orioles announced the hiring of <a href="/wiki/Dan_Duquette" title="Dan Duquette">Dan Duquette</a> as the vice president of baseball operations (<i>de facto</i> GM) in the hopes of turning the corner.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Return_to_success_.282012.E2.80.932017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_success_(2012\xe2\x80\x932017)">Return to success (2012\xe2\x80\x932017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Return to success (2012\xe2\x80\x932017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_season">2012 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 2012 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2012 Baltimore Orioles season">2012 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>The Orioles finished the first half of the 2012 season with a winning record for only the second time since going wire to wire in 1997, with a record of 45\xe2\x80\x9340 before the All-Star break. On May 6, the Orioles played a 17-inning game against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2012 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a>, the first game since 1925 in which both teams used a position player as a pitcher. The Orioles won that game, and designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Chris_Davis_(baseball)" title="Chris Davis (baseball)">Chris Davis</a> received the win. The Orioles won their 81st game on September 13, ending the streak of 14 straight years with a losing record, as well as ensuring that the team would spend the entire year with a record of .500 or higher. On September 16, they won their 82nd game, securing the first season with a winning record since 1997.\n</p><p>On September 21, closer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Johnson_(right-handed_pitcher)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jim Johnson (right-handed pitcher)">Jim Johnson</a> earned his 46th save of the season, setting a new Orioles franchise record for saves by one pitcher in a single season. It was previously held by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Myers" title="Randy Myers">Randy Myers</a>, who had 45 saves in 1997. Johnson became the tenth player to record 50 saves in Major League history. He finished the regular season with 51 saves.\n</p><p>With the win against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> on September 30 and the loss of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Los Angeles Angels</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2012 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> in the second game of a doubleheader, the Orioles clinched a playoff berth. This season marked the Orioles return to postseason play.\n</p><p>The Orioles finished the regular season in second place in the AL East with a record of 93\xe2\x80\x9369, reversing the 69\xe2\x80\x9393 record from the previous year. Despite a poor run differential (+7, the lowest of all playoff teams in 2012), they benefited from a 29\xe2\x80\x939 record in games decided by one run and a 16\xe2\x80\x932 record in extra-inning games. They went on the road to face the team that finished first in the Wild Card race, the Texas Rangers for a <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2012 American League Wild Card Game">one-game playoff series</a> on October 5, winning 5\xe2\x80\x931 to advance to the <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Division_Series" title="2012 American League Division Series">ALDS</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2012_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2012 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a> on October 7.\n</p><p>The season was also distinctive for the fact that Orioles became the only team in MLB history, since 1900, never to have lost a game due to an opponent\'s walk-off hit.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Despite a regular season of avoiding walk-off losses, they lost in Game 3 of the ALDS when Yankee <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Iba%C3%B1ez" title="Ra\xc3\xbal Iba\xc3\xb1ez">Ra\xc3\xbal Iba\xc3\xb1ez</a> hit his own record-setting, game-winning home run in the bottom of the 12th inning. The Orioles would lose the 2012 ALDS in five games.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_season">2013 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 2013 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2013 Baltimore Orioles season">2013 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>During the home opener on April 5, first baseman <a href="/wiki/Chris_Davis_(baseball)" title="Chris Davis (baseball)">Chris Davis</a> set a new MLB record with 16 RBI\'s during the first four games of a season, as well as becoming the fourth player ever to hit home runs in the first four games, including a grand slam in the fourth. On September 13, Davis hit his 50th home run of the season, against the <a href="/wiki/2013_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2013 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a>, tying <a href="/wiki/Brady_Anderson" title="Brady Anderson">Brady Anderson</a> for the most home runs in Orioles history. Davis would break Anderson\'s record four days later against the <a href="/wiki/2013_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2013 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a>. His 51st home run also tied Anderson\'s record of 92 extra-base hits in a single season, a record he would again break four days later. Davis would go on to finish the season with 53 home runs.\n</p><p>On September 18, the Orioles played their 114th errorless game of the season, setting a new MLB record for the most errorless games in one season since 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> They played 119&#160;games without an error, ending on September 27.\n</p><p>On September 20, the Orioles played the <a href="/wiki/2013_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2013 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a> in an 18 inning game that lasted 6&#160;hours, 54&#160;minutes, a new record for the longest game in terms of time for both franchises, as well as innings for the Rays. The Rays won 5\xe2\x80\x934.\n</p><p>While the Orioles would ultimately miss the playoffs in 2013, they finished with a record of 85\xe2\x80\x9377, tying the <a href="/wiki/2013_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2013 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> for third place in the AL East. By posting winning records in 2012 and 2013, the Orioles achieved the feat of back-to-back winning seasons for the first time since 1996 and 1997.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_season">2014 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 2014 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2014 Baltimore Orioles season">2014 Baltimore Orioles season</a></div>\n<p>On September 16, the Orioles clinched the division for the first time since 1997 with a win against the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> as well as making it back to the postseason for the second time in three years. The Orioles finished the 2014 season with a 96\xe2\x80\x9366 record and went on to sweep the Detroit Tigers in the <a href="/wiki/2014_American_League_Division_Series" title="2014 American League Division Series">ALDS</a>. Notably, the three Tigers starters were winners of the previous 3 AL <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a>; <a href="/wiki/Max_Scherzer" title="Max Scherzer">Max Scherzer</a> (2013), <a href="/wiki/Justin_Verlander" title="Justin Verlander">Justin Verlander</a> (2011), and <a href="/wiki/David_Price_(baseball)" title="David Price (baseball)">David Price</a> (2012). The O\'s were then in turn swept by the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2014 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_season">2015 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 2015 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On April 26, the Orioles scored 18 runs against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, the most runs they had scored in a single game, since they defeated the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> 18\xe2\x80\x939<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> on April 19, 2006. The Orioles beat the Red Sox 18\xe2\x80\x937.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On June 16, the Orioles scored 19 runs against the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, making it the most runs the Orioles have scored since earlier in the season against the Red Sox. The Orioles had 8 home runs during the game, a franchise record.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The team then later got their 5000th win as the Orioles on June 28 with a shutout 4\xe2\x80\x930 win over the Indians. On August 16, the Orioles defeated the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> 18\xe2\x80\x932, during which the team tied a franchise record for hits in a single game with 26.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On September 11, the Orioles rallied from a two-run deficit of 6\xe2\x80\x934 in the bottom of the 8th inning,  against the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>. The Orioles won the game 14\xe2\x80\x938. The rally included left fielder <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Reimold" title="Nolan Reimold">Nolan Reimold</a> and designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Steve_Clevenger" title="Steve Clevenger">Steve Clevenger</a> both hitting their first career grand slams, making the Orioles the only franchise in the history of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> to hit multiple grand slams in the same inning in two different games, the last time being in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On September 30, in a reverse of fortune, the Toronto Blue Jays clinched the AL East with a win over the Orioles in Baltimore where they watched the Orioles celebrate their division title clinch the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Response_to_2015_unrest">Response to 2015 unrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Response to 2015 unrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>\n<p>Out of an abundance of caution, the Baltimore Orioles announced the postponement of the April 27 and 28 games against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> following <a href="/wiki/2015_Baltimore_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Baltimore riots">violent riots</a> in West Baltimore following the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Freddie_Gray" title="Death of Freddie Gray">death of Freddie Gray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Following the announcement of the second postponement, the Orioles also announced that the third game in the series scheduled for Wednesday, April 29 was to be closed to the public and would be televised only,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> apparently the first time in 145 years of Major League Baseball that a game had no spectators and breaking the previous 131-year-old record for lowest paid attendance to an official game (the previous record being 6.) <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The Orioles beat the White Sox, 8\xe2\x80\x932.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Orioles said the make-up games would be played Thursday, May 28, as a double-header. In addition, the weekend games against the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> was moved to <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Field" title="Tropicana Field">the Rays\' home stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a> where Baltimore played as the home team.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniform">Uniform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Uniform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png/220px-ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png/330px-ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png/440px-ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ALE-Uniform-Orioles.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2012 uniforms. Left to right: Home, Away, Saturday (away with gray pants), Friday (away with gray pants.).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Orioles\' home uniform is white with the word "Orioles" written across the chest. The road uniform is gray with the word "Baltimore" written across the chest. A long campaign of several decades was waged by numerous fans and sportswriters to return the name of the city to the "away" jerseys which was used since the 1950s and had been formerly dropped during the 1970s era of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Bennett_Williams" title="Edward Bennett Williams">Edward Bennett Williams</a> when the ownership was continuing to market the team also to fans in the nation\'s capital region after the moving of the former <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">Washington Senators</a> in 1971. After several decades, approximately 20% of the team\'s attendance came from the metro Washington area. An alternate uniform is black with the word "Orioles" written across the chest. The Orioles wear their black alternate jerseys for Friday night games with the alternate "O\'s" cap, whether at home or on the road; the cartoon bird batting helmet is still used with this uniform (see description on home and road design).\n</p><p>For 2012, the team unveiled its new uniforms. There was a change to the cap insignia, with the cartoon Oriole returning. Home caps are white in front and black at the back with an orange bill, while the road caps are all black on top with an orange bill. The Orioles also introduced a new alternate orange uniform to be worn on Saturday home games throughout the 2012 season.\n</p><p>In 2013, ESPN ran a "Battle of the Uniforms" contest between all 30 Major League clubs. Despite using a ranking system that had the Orioles as a #13 seed, the Birds beat the #1 seed Cardinals in the championship round.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 27, 2014, the Orioles announced since their win in New York against the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> they will wear their \'new orange\' jerseys every Saturday for the rest of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2014 Baltimore Orioles season">2014 season</a> both home and away. They have since continued to wear the orange jerseys on most Saturday road games.\n</p><p>For 2017, the Orioles began to use their batting practice caps for select games with the black uniforms. The aforementioned caps resemble their regular road caps save for the black bill.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television_coverage">Radio and television coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Radio and television coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Baltimore_Orioles_broadcasters" title="List of Baltimore Orioles broadcasters">List of Baltimore Orioles broadcasters</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In Baltimore, Orioles games on radio can be heard over <a href="/wiki/WJZ-FM" title="WJZ-FM">WJZ-FM</a> (105.7&#160;FM). <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hunter_(sportscaster)" title="Jim Hunter (sportscaster)">Jim Hunter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Angel" title="Joe Angel">Joe Angel</a> alternate as <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcers. WJZ-FM also feeds the games to a <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles_Radio_Network" title="Baltimore Orioles Radio Network">network</a> of 36 stations, covering Washington, D.C. and all or portions of Maryland, Pennsylvania, Delaware, Virginia, West Virginia, and North Carolina.\n</p><p>WJZ-FM is in its second stint as the Orioles\' flagship radio outlet; the station had carried the team previously from 2007 through 2010. Previous radio flagships for the Orioles have been <a href="/wiki/WCBM" title="WCBM">WCBM</a> (680 AM) from 1954 to 1956, and again for the 1987 season; <a href="/wiki/WBAL_(AM)" title="WBAL (AM)">WBAL</a> (1090 AM) over three separate stints (1957 to 1978, 1988 to 2006, and 2011 to 2014); and WFBR (1300 AM, now <a href="/wiki/WJZ_(AM)" title="WJZ (AM)">WJZ</a>) from 1979 through 1986.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Sports_Network" title="Mid-Atlantic Sports Network">Mid-Atlantic Sports Network</a> (MASN), co-owned by the Orioles and the Washington Nationals, is the team\'s exclusive television broadcaster. MASN airs almost the entire slate of regular season games. Some exceptions include <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on Fox">Saturday games</a> on either <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> (via its Baltimore affiliate, <a href="/wiki/WBFF" title="WBFF">WBFF</a>) or <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_1" title="Fox Sports 1">Fox Sports 1</a>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ESPN" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on ESPN">Sunday Night Baseball</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>. Many MASN telecasts in conflict with Nationals\' game telecasts air on an alternate MASN2 feed.\n</p><p>Veteran sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Gary_Thorne" title="Gary Thorne">Gary Thorne</a> is the current lead television announcer, with <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hunter_(sportscaster)" title="Jim Hunter (sportscaster)">Jim Hunter</a> as his backup along with Hall of Fame member and former Orioles pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jim_Palmer" title="Jim Palmer">Jim Palmer</a> and former Oriole infielder <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bordick" title="Mike Bordick">Mike Bordick</a> as color analysts, who almost always work separately. All telecasts on MASN and WJZ-TV are shown in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high-definition</a>.\n</p><p>As part of the settlement of a television broadcast rights dispute with <a href="/wiki/Comcast_SportsNet_Mid-Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Comcast SportsNet Mid-Atlantic">Comcast SportsNet Mid-Atlantic</a>, the Orioles severed their Comcast ties at the end of the 2006 season. Comcast SportsNet had been the Orioles\' cable partner since 1984, when it was Home Team Sports.\n</p><p>WJZ-TV was the Orioles\' broadcast TV home, completing its latest stint from 1994 through 2017. Since MASN acquired rights in 2007, its coverage was <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">simulcast</a> on WJZ-TV under the branding "MASN on WJZ 13". MASN elected not to syndicate any Orioles or <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> games to broadcast television for the 2018 season, marking the first time since the Orioles\' arrival that their games are not on local broadcast television.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously, WJZ-TV carried the team from their arrival in Baltimore in 1954 through 1978. In the first four seasons, WJZ-TV shared coverage with Baltimore\'s other two stations, <a href="/wiki/WMAR-TV" title="WMAR-TV">WMAR-TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/WBAL-TV" title="WBAL-TV">WBAL-TV</a>. The games moved to WMAR from 1979 through 1993 before returning to WJZ-TV.  From 1994 to 2009, some Orioles games aired on <a href="/wiki/WNUV" title="WNUV">WNUV</a>. \n</p><p>Six former Oriole franchise radio announcers have received the Hall of Fame\'s <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> for excellence in broadcasting: <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Thompson" title="Chuck Thompson">Chuck Thompson</a> (who was also the voice of the old NFL <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Baltimore_Colts" title="History of the Baltimore Colts">Baltimore Colts</a>); <a href="/wiki/Jon_Miller" title="Jon Miller">Jon Miller</a> (now with the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>); <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Harwell" title="Ernie Harwell">Ernie Harwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herb_Carneal" title="Herb Carneal">Herb Carneal</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bob_Murphy_(announcer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Murphy (announcer)">Bob Murphy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a> (as a St. Louis Browns announcer in the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>).\n</p><p>Other former Baltimore announcers include <a href="/wiki/Josh_Lewin" title="Josh Lewin">Josh Lewin</a> (currently with <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bill_O%27Donnell_(sportscaster)" title="Bill O&#39;Donnell (sportscaster)">Bill O\'Donnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Marr" title="Tom Marr">Tom Marr</a>, Scott Garceau, <a href="/wiki/Mel_Proctor" title="Mel Proctor">Mel Proctor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Reghi" title="Michael Reghi">Michael Reghi</a>, former major league catcher <a href="/wiki/Buck_Martinez" title="Buck Martinez">Buck Martinez</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> play-by-play), and former Oriole players including Brooks Robinson, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Flanagan_(baseball)" title="Mike Flanagan (baseball)">Mike Flanagan</a> and outfielder <a href="/wiki/John_Lowenstein" title="John Lowenstein">John Lowenstein</a>. In 1991, the Orioles experimented with longtime TV writer/producer <a href="/wiki/Ken_Levine_(TV_personality)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ken Levine (TV personality)">Ken Levine</a> as a play-by-play broadcaster. Levine was best noted for his work on TV shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/Cheers" title="Cheers">Cheers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/M*A*S*H_(TV_series)" title="M*A*S*H (TV series)">M*A*S*H</a></i>, but only lasted one season in the Orioles broadcast booth.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_traditions">Musical traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Musical traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id=".22O.21.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;O!&quot;">"O!"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: &quot;O!&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since its introduction at games by the "Roar from 34", led by <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bill_Hagy" title="Wild Bill Hagy">Wild Bill Hagy</a> and others, in the late 1970s, it has been a tradition at Orioles games for fans to yell out the "Oh" in the line "Oh, say does that Star-Spangled Banner yet wave" in "<a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">The Star-Spangled Banner</a>". "The Star-Spangled Banner" has special meaning to Baltimore historically, as it was written during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baltimore" title="Battle of Baltimore">Battle of Baltimore</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Scott_Key" title="Francis Scott Key">Francis Scott Key</a>, a Baltimorean. "O" is not only short for "Oriole", but the vowel is also a stand-out aspect of the <a href="/wiki/Baltimorese" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimorese">Baltimorean accent</a>.\n</p><p>The tradition is often carried out at other sporting events, both professional or amateur, and even sometimes at non-sporting events where the anthem is played, throughout the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Baltimore\xe2\x80\x93Washington metropolitan area">Baltimore/Washington area</a> and beyond. Fans in <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk, Virginia</a>, chanted "O!" even before the <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Tides" title="Norfolk Tides">Tides</a> became an Orioles affiliate. The practice caught some attention in the spring of 2005, when fans performed the "O!" cry at <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> games at <a href="/wiki/RFK_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="RFK Stadium">RFK Stadium</a>. The "O!" chant is also common at sporting events for the various <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins" title="Maryland Terrapins">Maryland Terrapins</a> teams at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland, College Park</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a>\'s induction into the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a>, the crowd, composed mostly of Orioles fans, carried out the "O!" tradition during <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gwynn" title="Tony Gwynn">Tony Gwynn</a>\'s daughter\'s rendition of "The Star-Spangled Banner." Additionally, a faint but audible "O!" could be heard on the television broadcast of Barack Obama\'s pre-inaugural visit to Baltimore as the National Anthem played before his entrance. A resounding "O!" bellowed from the nearly 30,000 Ravens fans that attended the November 21, 2010, away game at the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Stadium" title="Bank of America Stadium">Bank of America Stadium</a> in Charlotte, North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> A similar loud "O!" was heard from fans attending <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII" title="Super Bowl XLVII">Super Bowl XLVII</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The "O!" chant was also heard during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, when Baltimore native <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phelps" title="Michael Phelps">Michael Phelps</a> received one of his gold medals on August 9, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years, when the Orioles host the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a>, fans have begun to shout out the multiple instances of the word "O" in <i>"<a href="/wiki/O_Canada" title="O Canada">O Canada</a></i>". <a href="/wiki/Washington_Capitals" title="Washington Capitals">Washington Capitals</a> fans will do the same when they play one of the NHL\'s Canadian teams.\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22Thank_God_I.27m_a_Country_Boy.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Thank_God_I\'m_a_Country_Boy&quot;">"Thank God I\'m a Country Boy"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: &quot;Thank God I&#039;m a Country Boy&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It has been an Orioles tradition since 1975 to play <a href="/wiki/John_Denver" title="John Denver">John Denver</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Thank_God_I%27m_a_Country_Boy" title="Thank God I&#39;m a Country Boy">Thank God I\'m a Country Boy</a>" during the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-inning_stretch" title="Seventh-inning stretch">seventh-inning stretch</a>.\n</p><p>In the edition of July 5, 2007, of Baltimore\'s weekly sports publication <i>Press Box</i>, an article by Mike Gibbons covered the details of how this tradition came to be.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> During "Thank God I\'m a Country Boy", Charlie Zill, then an usher, would put on overalls, a straw hat, and false teeth and dance around the club level section (244) that he tended to. He also has an orange violin that spins for the fiddle solos. He went by the name Zillbilly and had done the skit from the 1999 season until shortly before he died in early 2013. During a nationally televised game on September 20, 1997, Denver himself danced to the song atop the Orioles\' dugout, one of his final public appearances before dying in a plane crash three weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22Orioles_Magic.22_and_other_songs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Orioles_Magic&quot;_and_other_songs">"Orioles Magic" and other songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: &quot;Orioles Magic&quot; and other songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Songs from notable games in the team\'s history include "<a href="/wiki/One_Moment_in_Time" title="One Moment in Time">One Moment in Time</a>" for Cal Ripken\'s record-breaking game in 1995, as well as the theme from <i><a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_(film)" title="Pearl Harbor (film)">Pearl Harbor</a></i>, "There You\'ll Be" by <a href="/wiki/Faith_Hill" title="Faith Hill">Faith Hill</a>, during his final game in 2001. The theme from <i><a href="/wiki/Field_of_Dreams" title="Field of Dreams">Field of Dreams</a></i> was played at the last game at Memorial Stadium in 1991, and the song "Magic to Do" from the stage musical <i><a href="/wiki/Pippin_(musical)" title="Pippin (musical)">Pippin</a></i> was used that season to commemorate "Orioles Magic" on 33rd Street. During the Orioles\' heyday in the 1970s, a club song, appropriately titled "Orioles Magic (Feel It Happen)", was composed by Walt Woodward,<sup id="cite_ref-BaltSun_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaltSun-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and played when the team ran out until Opening Day of 2008. Since then, the song (a favorite among all fans, who appreciated its references to <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bill_Hagy" title="Wild Bill Hagy">Wild Bill Hagy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earl_Weaver" title="Earl Weaver">Earl Weaver</a>) is only played (along with a video featuring several Orioles stars performing the song) after wins. <a href="/wiki/Seven_Nation_Army" title="Seven Nation Army">Seven Nation Army</a> is played as a hype song while the fans chant the signature bass riff as a rally cry during key moments of a game or after a walk-off hit.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_First_Army_Band">The First Army Band</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: The First Army Band">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the Orioles\' final homestand of the season, it is a tradition to display a replica of the 15-star, 15-stripe <a href="/wiki/American_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="American flag">American flag</a> at Camden Yards. Prior to 1992, the 15-star, 15-stripe flag flew from Memorial Stadium\'s center-field flagpole in place of the 50-star, 13-stripe flag during the final homestand. Since the move to Camden Yards, the former flag has been displayed on the batters\' eye. During the Orioles\' final home game of the season, <a href="/wiki/The_United_States_Army_Field_Band" class="mw-redirect" title="The United States Army Field Band">The United States Army Field Band</a> from <a href="/wiki/Fort_George_G._Meade" title="Fort George G. Meade">Fort Meade</a> performs the <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">National Anthem</a> prior to the start of the game. The Band has also played the National Anthem at the finales of three <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> in which the Orioles played in: <a href="/wiki/1970_World_Series" title="1970 World Series">1970</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series" title="1971 World Series">1971</a> and <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Series" title="1979 World Series">1979</a>. They are introduced as the "First Army Band" during the pregame ceremonies.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="PA_announcer">PA announcer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: PA announcer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>For 23&#160;years, <a href="/wiki/Rex_Barney" title="Rex Barney">Rex Barney</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Public_address" class="mw-redirect" title="Public address">PA announcer</a> for the Orioles. His voice became a fixture of both Memorial Stadium and Camden Yards, and his expression "Give that fan a contract", uttered whenever a fan caught a <a href="/wiki/Foul_ball" title="Foul ball">foul ball</a>, was one of his trademarks&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the other being his distinct "Thank Yooooou..." following every announcement. (He was also known on occasion to say "Give that fan an error" after a dropped foul ball.) Barney died on August 12, 1997, and in his honor that night\'s game at Camden Yards against the Oakland Athletics was held without a public\xe2\x80\x93address announcer.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barney was replaced as Camden Yards\' PA announcer by Dave McGowan, who held the position until December 2011.\n</p><p>Lifelong Orioles fan and former <a href="/wiki/MLB_Fan_Cave" title="MLB Fan Cave">MLB Fan Cave</a> resident Ryan Wagner is the current PA announcer. He was chosen out of a field of more than 670 applicants in the 2011\xe2\x80\x9312 offseason.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Postseason_appearances">Postseason appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Postseason appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Of the eight original American League teams, the Orioles were the last of the eight to win the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, doing so in <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966</a> with its four\xe2\x80\x93game sweep of the heavily favored <a href="/wiki/1966_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1966 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>. When the Orioles were the St. Louis Browns, they played in only one World Series, the <a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944 matchup</a> against their Sportsman\'s Park tenants, the <a href="/wiki/1944_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1944 St. Louis Cardinals season">Cardinals</a>. The Orioles won the first-ever <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> in 1969, and in 2012 the Orioles beat the Texas Rangers in the inaugural American League <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild-card_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball wild-card game">Wild Card game</a>, where for the first time two Wild Card teams faced each other during postseason play.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" cellspacing="2">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th Frick Award (broadcasters only)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Ford C. Frick Award</span></a> recipients\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background-color: #DD4926; color: #FFFFFF; text-align: center;">Affiliation according to the National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<table style="margin: 1em auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Herb_Carneal" title="Herb Carneal">Herb Carneal</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Bob_Murphy_(announcer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Murphy (announcer)">Bob Murphy</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Milo_Hamilton" title="Milo Hamilton">Milo Hamilton</a><br /><a href="/wiki/J._Roy_Stockton" title="J. Roy Stockton</a>*<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ernie_Harwell" title="Ernie Harwell">Ernie Harwell</a><br /><b><a href="/wiki/Chuck_Thompson" title="Chuck Thompson">Chuck Thompson</a></b>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jon_Miller" title="Jon Miller">Jon Miller</a>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><b>Names in bold</b> received the award based primarily on their work as broadcasters for the Orioles or Browns.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li>*Since J. Taylor Spink award.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>\n<p>The Orioles will only retire a number when a player has been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Fame</a> with <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a> being the only exception.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;N 1&#93;</a></sup> However, the Orioles have placed moratoriums on other former Orioles\' numbers following their deaths (see note below).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> To date, the Orioles have retired the following numbers:\n</p>\n<table style="white-space:nowrap"><tbody><tr><td>\n<table style="float:left; Miller</a> (1965)</li>\n<li>Most relief points: 131, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Myers" title="Randy Myers">Randy Myers</a> (1997)</li>\n<li>Most innings pitched by reliever: 140.1, <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Stewart" title="Sammy Stewart">Sammy Stewart</a> (1983)</li>\n<li>Most consecutive wins: 15, <a href="/wiki/Dave_McNally" title="Dave McNally">Dave McNally</a> (April 12, 1969 \xe2\x80\x93 August 3, 1969)</li>\n<li>Most consecutive losses: 10, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Tibbs" title="Jay Tibbs">Jay Tibbs</a> (July 10, 1988 \xe2\x80\x93 October 1, 1988)</li>\n<li>Most consecutive losses, start of season: 8, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Boddicker" title="Mike Boddicker">Mike Boddicker</a> (1988) and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Johnson_(baseball)" title="Jason Johnson (baseball)">Jason Johnson</a> (2000)</li>\n<li>Most wins vs. one club: 6, <a href="/wiki/Wally_Bunker" title="Wally Bunker">Wally Bunker</a> vs. Kansas City (1964)</li>\n<li>Most losses vs. one club: 5 <a href="/wiki/Don_Larsen" title="Don Larsen">Don Larsen</a> vs. White Sox (1954), <a href="/wiki/Joe_Coleman_(1950s_pitcher)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joe Coleman (1950s pitcher)">Joe Coleman</a> vs. Yankees (1954), and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wilson_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jimmy Wilson (baseball)">Jim Wilson</a> vs. Cleveland (1955)</li>\n<li>Most wins by opponent: 6, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Pettitte" title="Andy Pettitte">Andy Pettitte</a>, Yankees (2003) and <a href="/wiki/Bud_Daley" title="Bud Daley">Bud Daley</a>, Kansas City (1959)</li>\n<li>Most losses by opponent: 5, <a href="/wiki/Ned_Garver" title="Ned Garver">Ned Garver</a>, Kansas City (1957), <a href="/wiki/Dick_Stigman" title="Dick Stigman">Dick Stigman</a>, Minnesota (1963), <a href="/wiki/Stan_Williams_(baseball)" title="Stan Williams (baseball)">Stan Williams</a>, Cleveland (1969), and <a href="/wiki/Catfish_Hunter" title="Catfish Hunter">Catfish Hunter</a>, Yankees (1976)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_the_Washington_Nationals">Rivalry with the Washington Nationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Rivalry with the Washington Nationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Orioles have a burgeoning regional rivalry<sup id="cite_ref-Orioles-Nats_weekend_series_gives_beltway_something_to_be_excited_about_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orioles-Nats_weekend_series_gives_beltway_something_to_be_excited_about-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beltway_Series_2011:_Birdland_Bias_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beltway_Series_2011:_Birdland_Bias-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> nicknamed the <a href="/wiki/Beltway_Series" title="Beltway Series">Beltway Series</a> or Battle of the Beltways. Baltimore currently leads the series with a 26\xe2\x80\x9320 record over the Nationals.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ripken\'s number was retired on October 6, 2001, in a ceremony moments before his last professional game.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Orioles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation pressrelease"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mlb.com/orioles/news/orioles-announce-uniform-changes-for-2012/c-25976148">"Orioles announce uniform changes for 2012"</a>. <i>Orioles.com</i> (Press release). <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a>.
